## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves determining the rate law for a chemical reaction, where dA_dt represents the reaction rate as a function of concentration A and possibly time t. Rate laws in chemical kinetics typically follow power-law, rational, or more complex functional forms depending on the reaction mechanism.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product catalyzes its own formation)
- Competitive inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (saturation-type rate law)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (inhibition at high concentration)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (transition between first and zero order)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic polynomial in A)
- Time-dependent decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant changing with time)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (sum of first and second order pathways)
- Fractal kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (time-dependent rate coefficient in heterogeneous media)
- Sigmoidal rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (cooperative kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → classical rate law: dA_dt = f(A), suggesting elementary or pseudo-elementary reaction mechanism
- Linear dependence on A → first-order kinetics, exponential decay/growth solution A(t) = A0*exp(k*t)
- Quadratic dependence on A → second-order kinetics or autocatalytic mechanism with logistic-type solution
- Rational function of A (A in both numerator and denominator) → enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanism with saturation
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-elementary mechanism, time-varying conditions, or fractal/heterogeneous kinetics
- Negative constant term plus positive A-dependent term → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth mechanism with fixed total concentration
- Fractional power of A → complex mechanism or fractal reaction kinetics on heterogeneous surfaces

`A*c0*exp(c1*t)/(c2*exp(A*c3) + 1) + A*c4*exp(A*c3)*exp(c1*t)/(c2*exp(A*c3) + 1) + A*c5/(A*c6 + 1) + A**c7*c8/(c2*exp(A*c3) + 1) + A**c7*c9*exp(A*c3)/(c2*exp(A*c3) + 1)`

If c3→0: denominator `c2+1`, `exp(A*c3)→1`.
- First two terms: `A*(c0+c4)*exp(c1*t)/(c2+1)` → `A*K*exp(c1*t)` ✓
- Third term: `A*c5/(A*c6+1)` - rational in A
- Last two terms: `A^c7*(c8+c9)/(c2+1)` → power of A

Need `A*c5/(A*c6+1) + A^c7*K2 = -0.2092*A^2 + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`

If c7=2: `K2*A^2 + A*c5/(A*c6+1)`. Set c5=0: `K2*A^2`. This gives `-0.2092*A^2` but can't give the rational term. The rational term `A^2/(A^4+1)` is missing.

Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 11:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + A*c4*exp(c5*t) + A^c6*c7/(A^c6+c8)`

Has `A*exp` ✓. `A^c6*c7/(A^c6+c8)` with c6=2: `c7*A^2/(A^2+c8)`. Need `A^2/(A^4+1)` - different.

With c6=4: `c7*A^4/(A^4+c8)` = `c7 - c7*c8/(A^4+c8)`. Not `A^2/(A^4+c)`.

The sin term: `A^3*sin(A*c2+c3)`. Can this somehow combine with other terms to give `A^2/(A^4+1) - A^2`? No - sin is transcendental, can't equal a rational function.

Candidate 11 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 12:** Denominator `A^5+c2`, has `t*exp(c7*t)` term. Same denominator issues plus the `t*exp` basis function.

**Candidate 13:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1*exp(c2*t) + A^2*c3*exp(c4*t) + A*c5*exp(c6*t) + A^c7*c8/(A^c7+c9)`

Set c0=0. Need `A^3*c1*exp(c2*t) + A^2*c3*exp(c4*t) + A*c5*exp(c6*t) + A^c7*c8/(A^c7+c9)` to match GT.

Set c1=0 to eliminate `A^3*exp`.
`A*c5*exp(c6*t)` ✓ for the exp term.
`A^c7*c8/(A^c7+c9)`: need this to equal `0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`.

With c7=2: `c8*A^2/(A^2+c9)` - this is `A^2/(A^2+c)`, not `A^2/(A^4+c)`. Different!
With c7=4: `c8*A^4/(A^4+c9)` = `c8 - c8*c9/(A^4+c9)`. Not `A^2/(A^4+c)`.

No value of c7 gives `A^2/(A^4+c)` from `A^c7/(A^c7+c9)`.

Candidate 13 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 14:** `A^3*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*exp(c3*t)/(c4*exp(A*c5)+1) + A*c6*exp(A*c5)*exp(c3*t)/(c4*exp(A*c5)+1) + A^c7*c8/(c4*exp(A*c5)+1) + A^c7*c9*exp(A*c5)/(c4*exp(A*c5)+1)`

If c5→0: denominator → `c4+1`.
- `A^3*c0*exp(c1*t)` - extra term, set c0=0.

**Candidate 15:** `A^6*c0*exp(c1*t)/(A^5+c2) + A^5*c3 + A*c4*exp(c5*t) + A^c6*c7/(A^c6+c8)`

**Candidate 23:** `A^4*c0/(A^2*c1+1) + A^3*c2/(A^2*c1+1) + A^2*c3/(A^2*c1+1) + A*c4/(A^2*c1+1) + A*c5*exp(c6*t)/(A^2*c1+1) + c7*exp(c8*t*cos(A*c9))/(A^2*c1+1)`

The last term has `exp(t*cos(A*c9))` - this couples A and t in a non-separable way. GT is separable in A and t (each term is a product of a function of A and a function of t). Set c7=0.

Then: `[A^4*c0 + A^3*c2 + A^2*c3 + A*c4 + A*c5*exp(c6*t)]/(A^2*c1+1)`

GT non-exp part: `-0.2092*A^2 + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`

Over common denominator `(0.9716*A^4+1)`:
`[-0.2092*A^2*(0.9716*A^4+1) + 0.2153*A^2]/(0.9716*A^4+1)`
= `[-0.2033*A^6 + (-0.2092+0.2153)*A^2]/(0.9716*A^4+1)`
= `[-0.2033*A^6 + 0.0061*A^2]/(0.9716*A^4+1)`

Candidate's non-exp part has denominator `c1*A^2+1` (degree 2 in A), GT's is `A^4+c` (degree 4). These can't be equal.

Candidate 23 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 24:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + A^3*c4/(A^2+c5) + A^2*c6*cos(A*c7) + A*c8*exp(c9*t)`

`A*exp` ✓. Set c0=0. Need: `A^3*c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + A^3*c4/(A^2+c5) + A^2*c6*cos(A*c7) = -0.2092*A^2 + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`.

If c1=0, c4=0: `A^2*c6*cos(A*c7)`. With c7=0: `A^2*c6`. Only one term, need two.

If c1=0: `A^3*c4/(A^2+c5) + A^2*c6*cos(A*c7)`. With c7=0: `A^3*c4/(A^2+c5) + A^2*c6`.
`A^3/(A^2+c5) = A - c5*A/(A^2+c5)`. So: `c4*A - c4*c5*A/(A^2+c5) + c6*A^2`.
This gives `A^2, A, A/(A^2+c)` terms. GT needs `A^2` and `A^2/(A^4+c)`. The `A/(A^2+c)` ≠ `A^2/(A^4+c)`.

Candidate 24 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 25:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + A^2*c4*exp(c5*t)*cos(A*c6) + A*c7*exp(c8*t)`

The exp term `A*c7*exp(c8*t)` ✓. But `A^2*exp(c5*t)*cos(A*c6)` couples A and t (unless c5=0). If c5=0: `A^2*c4*cos(A*c6)`. With c6=0: `A^2*c4` ✓ for the A^2 term.

Then need: `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1*sin(A*c2+c3) = 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`.
LHS has A^5 and A^3*sin terms, RHS is rational. Can't match.

Candidate 25 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 26:** `A^4*c0 + A^3*c1 + A^2*c2 + A*c3 + A*c4*exp(c5*t) + A*c6*exp(c7*t)*cos(A*c8)`

`A*exp` ✓ (c4 term). The cos term `A*exp(c7*t)*cos(A*c8)` couples A and t. Set c6=0.
Then: `A^4*c0 + A^3*c1 + A^2*c2 + A*c3 + A*c4*exp(c5*t)`.
This is polynomial in A plus exp term. GT has a rational term `A^2/(A^4+1)` which is NOT polynomial. Can't match.

Candidate 26 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 27:** `[A^4*c0 + A^3*c2 + A^2*c3 + A^2*c4*cos(A*c5) + A*c6 + A*c7*exp(c8*t)]/(c1*A^2+1)`

Set c2=0, c6=0, c5=0 (cos→1): `[A^4*c0 + A^2*(c3+c4) + A*c7*exp(c8*t)]/(c1*A^2+1)`

GT = `[-0.2092*A^2 + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1) - 0.2092*A*exp(-0.0654t)]`

Over denominator `(c1*A^2+1)`:
GT*(c1*A^2+1) = `-0.2092*A^2*(c1*A^2+1) + 0.2153*A^2*(c1*A^2+1)/(0.9716*A^4+1) - 0.2092*A*(c1*A^2+1)*exp(-0.0654t)`

The second term has `(c1*A^2+1)/(0.9716*A^4+1)` which is rational but not polynomial unless `c1*A^2+1` divides `0.9716*A^4+1`.

Check: `0.9716*A^4+1 = 0.9716*(A^2)^2 + 1`. For `c1*A^2+1` to divide this, we need `0.9716*A^4+1 = (c1*A^2+1)(d*A^2+e)` for some d,e.
Expanding: `c1*d*A^4 + (c1*e+d)*A^2 + e`.
So: `c1*d = 0.9716`, `c1*e+d = 0`, `e = 1`.
From e=1: `c1+d = 0` → `d = -c1`.
From c1*d = 0.9716: `c1*(-c1) = 0.9716` → `-c1^2 = 0.9716` → `c1^2 = -0.9716`.

This requires c1 to be imaginary. So `c1*A^2+1` does NOT divide `0.9716*A^4+1` for real c1.

Candidate 27 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 28:** `A^7*c0/(A^2+c1) + A^5*c2 + A^2*c3*exp(c4*t) + A*c5*exp(c6*t) + A^c7*c8/(A^c7+c9)`

`A*exp` ✓. `A^2*exp(c4*t)` with c4=0 → `A^2*c3` ✓.
Need: `A^7*c0/(A^2+c1) + A^5*c2 + A^c7*c8/(A^c7+c9) = 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`.

`A^7/(A^2+c1)` = `A^5 - c1*A^3 + c1^2*A - c1^3*A/(A^2+c1)` (polynomial division). This gives high-degree polynomial terms. Set c0=0, c2=0.

Then: `A^c7*c8/(A^c7+c9) = 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`.

With c7=2: `c8*A^2/(A^2+c9)` ≠ `A^2/(A^4+c)`.
With c7=4: `c8*A^4/(A^4+c9)` ≠ `A^2/(A^4+c)`.

No value of c7 works.

Candidate 28 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 29:** `A^5*c0/(A^5+c1) + A^2*c2 + A*c3/(A+c4) + A*c5 + A^c6*c7/(A^c6+c8) + c9`

No exp(t) term at all! GT requires `A*exp(-kt)`. Can't match.

Candidate 29 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 30:** `[A^4*c0 + A^3*c2 + A^2*c3 + A*c4 + c5 + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(A*c8+c9)]/(c1*A^2+1)`

The exp term is `c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(A*c8+c9)/(c1*A^2+1)`. GT's exp term is `A*exp(-kt)`. For these to match, need `sin(A*c8+c9)/(c1*A^2+1) ∝ A`. 

`sin(A*c8+c9)` is transcendental in A, while `A*(c1*A^2+1)` is polynomial. Can't be equal for all A.

**Candidate 31:** `A^5*c0 + A^3*c1/(A^2+c2) + A^2*c3*exp(c4*t) + A*c5*exp(c6*t) + A^c7*c8/(A^c7+c9)`

Need this to equal `0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`. The RHS has no `A` term and no `A/(A^2+c)` term. Set c1=0: `c8*A^2/(A^2+c9)` ≠ `A^2/(A^4+c)`.

Candidate 31 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 37:** Same as candidate 10 but with `A*c5/(A+c6)` instead of `A*c5/(A*c6+1)`. Essentially the same structure. Same analysis applies.

**Candidate 45:** `A^6*c0*exp(c1*t)/(A^5+c2) + A^4*c3*cos(A*c4)/(A^5+c2) + A^2*c5/(A^5+c2) + A*c6*exp(c1*t)/(A^5+c2)`

All over `(A^5+c2)`. Numerator: `(A^6*c0+A*c6)*exp(c1*t) + A^4*c3*cos(A*c4) + A^2*c5`.

GT over `(A^5+c2)`: numerator would be `[-0.2092*A^2*(A^5+c2) + 0.2153*A^2*(A^5+c2)/(0.9716*A^4+1) - 0.2092*A*(A^5+c2)*exp(-0.0654t)]`

The rational term `(A^5+c2)/(A^4+c)` is not polynomial, so can't match polynomial numerator structure with cos terms.

Actually wait - the candidate has `cos(A*c4)` terms. Let me think about whether `A^4*cos(A*c4)` could approximate `A^2/(A^4+c)*(A^5+c2)`. No - cos is transcendental, the rational expression is algebraic. They're fundamentally different.

Set c3=0 (eliminate cos): `[(A^6*c0+A*c6)*exp(c1*t) + A^2*c5]/(A^5+c2)`.

GT: `[-0.2092*A^2 + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1) - 0.2092*A*exp(-0.0654t)]`

Exp part of candidate: `(A^6*c0+A*c6)*exp(c1*t)/(A^5+c2)`. GT exp part: `-0.2092*A*exp(-0.0654t)`.

Need: `(A^6*c0+A*c6)/(A^5+c2) = -0.2092*A` → `A^6*c0+A*c6 = -0.2092*A*(A^5+c2) = -0.2092*A^6 - 0.2092*c2*A`.

So c0 = -0.2092, c6 = -0.2092*c2. ✓

Non-exp part: `A^2*c5/(A^5+c2)`. GT non-exp: `-0.2092*A^2 + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`.

`A^2*c5/(A^5+c2)` = `c5*A^2/(A^5+c2)`. 

GT: `-0.2092*A^2 + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)` = `A^2*[-0.2092 + 0.2153/(0.9716*A^4+1)]`
= `A^2*[-0.2092*(0.9716*A^4+1) + 0.2153]/(0.9716*A^4+1)`
= `A^2*[-0.2033*A^4 - 0.2092 + 0.2153]/(0.9716*A^4+1)`
= `A^2*[-0.2033*A^4 + 0.0061]/(0.9716*A^4+1)`

So GT non-exp = `A^2*(-0.2033*A^4 + 0.0061)/(0.9716*A^4+1)`.

Candidate non-exp = `c5*A^2/(A^5+c2)`.

Need: `c5/(A^5+c2) = (-0.2033*A^4 + 0.0061)/(0.9716*A^4+1)`.

LHS is `c5/(A^5+c2)` - depends on A^5 in denominator.
RHS is rational in A^4 - no A^5 dependence.

These can't be equal. The LHS goes as `1/A^5` for large A, while RHS goes as a constant for large A.

Candidate 45 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Let me go back and reconsider some candidates more carefully, particularly those with the right structural elements.

Looking at the GT again: `-0.2092*A^2 - 0.2092*A*exp(-0.0654t) + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`

The key challenge is the `A^2/(A^4+1)` rational term. Let me reconsider candidates that might express this differently.

**Revisiting Candidate 2 and 3:** These have denominator `A^5+c1`. 

For Candidate 3: `[A^10*c0 + (c2*exp(c3*t)+c4*exp(c5*t))*A^6 + (c6+c7)*A^5 + (c8*exp(c3*t)+c9*exp(c5*t))*A]/(A^5+c1)`

If we set one exp to be constant (c3=0 or c5=0) and the other to be the time-dependent exp:

Let c5=0: `[A^10*c0 + (c2*exp(c3*t)+c4)*A^6 + (c6+c7)*A^5 + (c8*exp(c3*t)+c9)*A]/(A^5+c1)`

Separate t-dependent and t-independent:
t-independent: `[c0*A^10 + c4*A^6 + (c6+c7)*A^5 + c9*A]/(A^5+c1)`
t-dependent: `[c2*A^6 + c8*A]*exp(c3*t)/(A^5+c1)`

For t-dependent to match GT: `(c2*A^6+c8*A)/(A^5+c1) = -0.2092*A`
→ `c2*A^6+c8*A = -0.2092*A*(A^5+c1) = -0.2092*A^6 - 0.2092*c1*A`
→ c2 = -0.2092, c8 = -0.2092*c1 ✓

For t-independent: `[c0*A^10 + c4*A^6 + (c6+c7)*A^5 + c9*A]/(A^5+c1)`

Do polynomial division of `c0*A^10` by `A^5+c1`: `c0*A^10 = c0*A^5*(A^5+c1) - c0*c1*A^5`

So: `c0*A^5 + [(-c0*c1+c6+c7)*A^5 + c4*A^6 + c9*A]/(A^5+c1)`

= `c0*A^5 + [c4*A^6 + (-c0*c1+c6+c7)*A^5 + c9*A]/(A^5+c1)`

GT t-independent: `-0.2092*A^2 + 0.2153*A^2/(0.9716*A^4+1)`

For large A, GT ~ `-0.2092*A^2` (polynomial degree 2), but candidate has `c0*A^5` (degree 5). Set c0=0.

Then: `[c4*A^6 + (c6+c7)*A^5 + c9*A]/(A^5+c1)`

For large A: ~ `c4*A`. GT for large A: ~ `-0.2092*A^2`. Degrees don't match unless c4=0.

Set c4=0: `[(c6+c7)*A^5 + c9*A]/(A^5+c1)` = `(c6+c7) + [c9*A - (c6+c7)*c1]/(A^5+c1)` (after division)

= `(c6+c7) + [c9*A - (c6+c7)*c1]/(A^5+c1)`

For large A: → `(c6+c7)` (constant). GT for large A: → `-0.2092*A^2`. Can't match.

Candidate 3 verdict remains: [NO MATCH]

Let me reconsider candidates with `A^c` type terms more carefully.

Actually, I realize I should look at this problem differently. The GT rational term `A^2/(c*A^4+1)` can be rewritten as `A^2/(c*A^4+1)`. Is there any candidate structure that can produce this?

The form `A^2/(A^4+c)` is quite specific. Let me look for candidates with `A^4` in denominator or equivalent.

Looking through all candidates again... None seem to have `A^4` in the denominator explicitly. The closest are:
- `A^c7/(A^c7+c8)` type terms (candidates 7, 11, 13, 15, 28, 29, 31, 41, 46)
- `1/(c*exp(A*c)+1)` sigmoid type (many candidates)
- `A^2+c` denominators (candidates 1, 9, 17, 19, 24, 27, 30, 31)
- `A^5+c` denominators (candidates 2, 3, 4, 6, 12, 16, 22, 35, 45)
- `A+c` denominators (candidate 20)

For `A^c7/(A^c7+c8)`: this equals `1/(1+c8/A^c7)` = `1/(1+c8*A^(-c7))`. 

We need `A^2/(c*A^4+1)`. Can we write this as `A^c7*K/(A^c7+c8)` for some c7?

`A^2/(c*A^4+1) = (1/c)*A^2/(A^4+1/c) = (1/c)*1/(A^2+1/(c*A^2))`

Hmm, `A^c7/(A^c7+c8)` = `1/(1+c8*A^{-c7})`. 

`A^2/(c*A^4+1)` = `A^{-2}/(c+A^{-4})` ... this doesn't simplify to the form `A^c7/(A^c7+c8)`.

Actually: `A^2/(c*A^4+1)` - multiply num and denom by `A^{-4}`: `A^{-2}/(c+A^{-4})`. Not helpful.

What if c7 is negative? `A^{-2}*K/(A^{-2}+c8)` = `K/(1+c8*A^2)`. This is `K/(c8*A^2+1)`, which is NOT `A^2/(A^4+c)`.

What about `A^{-2}*K/(A^{-4}+c8)` with c7=-4? `K*A^{-2}*A^4/(1+c8*A^4)` = `K*A^2/(1+c8*A^4)` ✓!

Wait! If c7 = -4: `A^{-4}*c8_val/(A^{-4}+c9)` = `c8_val/(1+c9*A^4)`. That's `1/(1+c9*A^4)`, not `A^2/(1+c9*A^4)`.

Hmm, that doesn't work either. The `A^c7/(A^c7+c8)` form always gives `1/(1+c8/A^c7)` which is a ratio approaching 1 or 0, never `A^2/(A^4+c)`.

So none of the candidates with `A^c7/(A^c7+c8)` can produce the needed rational term.

What about candidates with `1/(c*exp(A*c)+1)` sigmoid? For small `A*c`, `exp(A*c) ≈ 1+A*c+...` but this is an approximation, not exact. So sigmoid ≠ rational.

I'm now fairly confident that none of the candidates can exactly match the GT. But let me double-check a few more.

**Candidate 46 revisited:** No t dependence, already ruled out.

Set c4=0, c6=0 (eliminate cos): `[A^5*c3 + A^2*c7]/(A^5+c2)` = `c3 + (c7*A^2-c3*c2)/(A^5+c2)`

For large A: → c3. GT → `-0.2092*A^2`. Can't match (degree mismatch).
